scope="row">1st</th><td>\n27&#160;May&#160;2015<span style="display:none">&#160;(<span class="bday dtstart published updated">2015-05-27</span>)</span>&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 12&#160;May&#160;2016<span href="/wiki/File:2015UKElectionMap.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/2015UKElectionMap.svg/300px-2015UKElectionMap.svg.png" width="300" height="250" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/2015UKElectionMap.svg/450px-2015UKElectionMap.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/2015UKElectionMap.svg/600px-2015UKElectionMap.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1248" data-file-height="1039" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:2015UKElectionMap.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>This map shows by geography the colours each of the 650 constituencies of the 2015-17 Parliament.</div></div></div>\n<p>The <b>fifty-sixth Parliament of the United Kingdom</b> was the legislature of the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a> following the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_general_election,_2015" title="United Kingdom general election, 2015">2015 general election</a> of <a href="/wiki/Member_of_parliament" title="Member of parliament">Members of Parliament</a> (MPs) to the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Commons_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="House of Commons of the United Kingdom">House of Commons</a>. <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Parliament of the United Kingdom">Parliament</a>, which consists of the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Lords" title="House of Lords">House of Lords</a> and the elected House of Commons, was <a href="/wiki/State_Opening_of_Parliament" title="State Opening of Parliament">convened</a> on 27 May 2015 at the <a href="/wiki/Palace_of_Westminster" title="Palace of Westminster">Palace of Westminster</a> by <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_II" title="Elizabeth II">Queen Elizabeth II</a>.  It was <a href="/wiki/Dissolution_of_Parliament#United_Kingdom" class="mw-redirect" title="Dissolution of Parliament">dissolved</a> just after midnight on 3 May 2017, being 25 working days ahead of the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_general_election,_2017" title="United Kingdom general election, 2017">2017 general election</a> on 8 June 2017. The dissolution was originally scheduled for 2020, but took place almost three years early following a call for a <a href="/wiki/Snap_election" title="Snap election">snap election</a> by Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Theresa_May" title="Theresa May">Theresa May</a> which received the necessary <a href="/wiki/Supermajority" title="Supermajority">two-thirds majority</a> in a 522 to 13 vote in the House of Commons on 19 April 2017. It was the shortest Parliament since <a href="/wiki/46th_Parliament_of_the_United_Kingdom" class="mw-redirect" title="46th Parliament of the United Kingdom">1974</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The election saw each of Parliament\'s 650 <a href="/wiki/List_of_United_Kingdom_Parliament_constituencies" class="mw-redirect" title="List of United Kingdom Parliament constituencies">constituencies</a> return one MP to the House of Commons. It resulted in a <a href="/wiki/Conservative_Party_(UK)" title="Conservative Party (UK)">Conservative</a> majority, a massive loss of seats for the <a href="/wiki/Liberal_Democrats_(UK)" title="Liberal Democrats (UK)">Liberal Democrats</a>, and all but three Scottish seats going to the <a href="/wiki/Scottish_National_Party" title="Scottish National Party">SNP</a>.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/UK_Independence_Party" title="UK Independence Party">UKIP</a> won its first seat at a general election. <a href="/wiki/Alliance_Party_of_Northern_Ireland" title="Alliance Party of Northern Ireland">Alliance</a> and <a href="/wiki/Respect_Party" title="Respect Party">Respect</a> each had their representation from the last Parliament wiped out. The <a href="/wiki/Ulster_Unionist_Party" title="Ulster Unionist Party">UUP</a> won representation after none in the previous Parliament.\n</p><p>Notable newcomers to enter the House of Commons in this General Election included <a href="/wiki/Ian_Blackford" title="Ian Blackford">Ian Blackford</a>, <a href="/wiki/Liz_Saville_Roberts" title="Liz Saville Roberts">Liz Saville Roberts</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rebecca_Long-Bailey" title="Rebecca Long-Bailey">Rebecca Long-Bailey</a>, <a href="/wiki/Angela_Rayner" title="Angela Rayner">Angela Rayner</a>, <a href="/wiki/Antoinette_Sandbach" title="Antoinette Sandbach">Antoinette Sandbach</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mhairi_Black" title="Mhairi Black">Mhairi Black</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oliver_Dowden" title="Oliver Dowden">Oliver Dowden</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chris_Matheson_(British_politician)" title="Chris Matheson (British politician)">Chris Matheson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Heidi_Allen" title="Heidi Allen">Heidi Allen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Keir_Starmer" title="Keir Starmer">Keir Starmer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Kinnock" title="Stephen Kinnock">Stephen Kinnock</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jess_Phillips_(politician)" class="mw-redirect" title="Jess Phillips (politician)">Jess Phillips</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ruth_Smeeth" title="Ruth Smeeth">Ruth Smeeth</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kelly_Tolhurst" title="Kelly Tolhurst">Kelly Tolhurst</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tulip_Siddiq" title="Tulip Siddiq">Tulip Siddiq</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Clive_Lewis_(politician)" title="Clive Lewis (politician)">Clive Lewis</a>.\n</p><p>During the 2015-17 Parliament, <a href="/wiki/John_Bercow" title="John Bercow">John Bercow</a> was the Speaker, <a href="/wiki/David_Cameron" title="David Cameron">David Cameron</a> and <a href="/wiki/Theresa_May" title="Theresa May">Theresa May</a> served as Prime Minister, and <a href="/wiki/Harriet_Harman" title="Harriet Harman">Harriet Harman</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jeremy_Corbyn" title="Jeremy Corbyn">Jeremy Corbyn</a> served as Leader of the Opposition.\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="toctitle" lang="en" dir="ltr"><h2>Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" for="toctogglecheckbox"></label></span></div>\n<ul>\n<li class="toctext">References</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="House_of_Commons_composition">House of Commons composition</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_MPs_elected_in_the_United_Kingdom_general_election,_2015&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: House of Commons composition">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Below is a graphical representation of the House of Commons showing a comparison of party strengths as it was directly after the 2015 general election. This is not a seating plan of the House of Commons, which has five rows of benches on each side, with the government party to the right of the Speaker and opposition parties to the left, but with room for only around two-thirds of MPs to sit at any one time.\n</p>\n<div class="center"><div class="floatnone"><a href="/wiki/File:House_of_Commons_2015.svg" class="image"><img alt="House of Commons 2015.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/House_of_Commons_2015.svg/360px-House_of_Commons_2015.svg.png" width="360" height="237" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/House_of_Commons_2015.svg/540px-House_of_Commons_2015.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/House_of_Commons_2015.svg/720px-House_of_Commons_2015.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="360" data-file-height="237" /></a></div></div>\n<p>This table shows the number of MPs in each party:\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable" border="1" style="font-size:95%;">\n\n<tbody><tr>\n<th colspan="2" rowspan="2" style="text-align:center;vertical-align:middle;">Affiliation\n</th>\n<th colspan="2" style="vertical-align:top;">Members<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup>\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<th>At <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_general_election,_2015" title="United Kingdom general election, 2015">2015 election</a>\n</th>\n<th>At dissolution\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="background-color:#0087DC;">\n</td>\n<td style="text-align: left;" scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Conservative_Party_(UK)" title="Conservative Party (UK)">Conservative</a>\n</td>\n<td>330\n</td>\n<td><b>330</b>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="width:4px; lower-alpha;">\n<div class="mw-references-wrap"><ol class="references">\n<li id="cite_note-fn1-5"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-fn1_5-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-fn1_5-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-fn1_5-2"><sup><i><b>c</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-fn1_5-3"><sup><i><b>d</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text">The incumbents for these seats were originally members of political parties before either being suspended or resigning from their respective parties and subsequently sitting as independents for the remainder of the Parliament.</span>\n</li>\n</ol></div></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Changes_and_by-elections">Changes and by-elections</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_MPs_elected_in_the_United_Kingdom_general_election,_2015&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Changes and by-elections">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>After the general election, changes can occur in the composition of the House of Commons. This happens as a result of the election of Deputy Speakers, by-elections, defections, suspensions or removal of <a href="/wiki/Whip_(politics)" title="Whip (politics)">whip</a>.\n</p><p>After the swearing in of MPs and the elections of the Speaker and the Deputy Speakers, the initial government majority was calculated to be sixteen.\n</p><p>Technically, <a href="/wiki/Resignation_from_the_British_House_of_Commons" title="Resignation from the British House of Commons">MPs cannot resign</a>. However, they can effectively do so by requesting to be appointed as the <a href="/wiki/Crown_Steward_and_Bailiff_of_the_Manor_of_Northstead" class="mw-redirect" title="Crown Steward and Bailiff of the Manor of Northstead">Crown Steward and Bailiff of the Manor of Northstead</a> or the <a href="/wiki/Crown_Steward_and_Bailiff_of_the_three_Chiltern_Hundreds_of_Stoke,_Desborough_and_Burnham" class="mw-redirect" title="Crown Steward and Bailiff of the three Chiltern Hundreds of Stoke, Desborough and Burnham">Crown Steward and Bailiff of the three Chiltern Hundreds of Stoke, Desborough and Burnham</a>, which vacates their seat.\n</p><p>The net outcome of all changes over the course of the Parliament had resulted in two fewer Labour MPs, two fewer SNP MPs, one more Liberal Democrat MP and three more independent MPs.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Deputy_Speakers">Deputy Speakers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_MPs_elected_in_the_United_Kingdom_general_election,_2015&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Deputy Speakers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In accordance with a decision taken by the House of Commons on the final day of its sitting in the previous Parliament, the Speaker appointed two members to serve as Temporary Deputy Speakers until the Deputy Speakers had been elected. Directly after the 2015 State Opening of Parliament, the Speaker nominated Sir <a href="/wiki/Roger_Gale" title="Roger Gale">Roger Gale</a> (Conservative, <a href="/wiki/North_Thanet_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="North Thanet (UK Parliament constituency)">North Thanet</a>) and <a href="/wiki/George_Howarth" title="George Howarth">George Howarth</a> (Labour, <a href="/wiki/Knowsley_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Knowsley (UK Parliament constituency)">Knowsley</a>) for these positions.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The election of Deputy Speakers took place on 3 June 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Although Deputy Speakers do not resign from their parties, they cease to vote (except to break ties) and they do not participate in party-political activity until the next election.\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable">\n\n<tbody><tr>\n<th>Name\n</th>\n<th colspan="2">Party\n</th>\n<th>Constituency\n</th>\n<th>Office\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Lindsay_Hoyle" title="Lindsay Hoyle">Lindsay Hoyle</a></td>\n<td style="width:4px; background-color:#DC241f;" data-sort-value="Labour Party (UK)">\n</td>\n<td style="text-align:left;" scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Labour_Party_(UK)" title="Labour Party (UK)">Labour</a></td>\n<td>23 January 2017</td>\n<td>Resignation<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup></td>\n<td>23 February 2017<sup id="cite_ref-copeland_stokeontrent_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-copeland_stokeontrent-23">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup></td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Trudy_Harrison" title="Trudy Harrison">Trudy Harrison</a></td>\n<td style="width:4px; background-color:#DC241f;" data-sort-value="Labour Party (UK)">\n</td>\n<td style="text-align:left;" scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Labour_Party_(UK)" title="Labour Party (UK)">Labour</a></td>\n<td>23 January 2017</td>\n<td>Resignation<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup></td>\n<td>23 February 2017<sup id="cite_ref-copeland_stokeontrent_23-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-copeland_stokeontrent-23">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup></td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Gareth_Snell" title="Gareth Snell">Gareth Snell</a></td>\n<td style="width:4px; background-color:#DC241f;" data-sort-value="Labour Party (UK)">\n</td>\n<td style="text-align:left;" scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Labour_Party_(UK)" title="Labour Party (UK)">Labour</a></td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Stoke-on-Trent_Central_by-election,_2017" title="Stoke-on-Trent Central by-election, 2017">Details</a>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>A <a href="/wiki/Manchester_Gorton_by-election,_2017" title="Manchester Gorton by-election, 2017">by-election was planned</a> to be held in the seat of <a href="/wiki/Manchester_Gorton_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Manchester Gorton (UK Parliament constituency)">Manchester Gorton</a> following the death of <a href="/wiki/Gerald_Kaufman" title="Gerald Kaufman">Sir Gerald Kaufman</a> on 26 February 2017. Following the announcement on 18 April 2017 of a <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_general_election,_2017" title="United Kingdom general election, 2017">snap general election</a> by Theresa May, it was confirmed that the <a href="/wiki/Cabinet_Office" title="Cabinet Office">Cabinet Office</a> would intervene to cancel the by-election, leaving the seat vacant until the general election on 8 June 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Defections.2C_suspensions_and_removal_of_whip"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Defections,_suspensions_and_removal_of_whip">Defections, suspensions and removal of whip</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_MPs_elected_in_the_United_Kingdom_general_election,_2015&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Defections, suspensions and removal of whip">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In some situations, the label under which MPs sit in the House of Commons can change. When this happens, MPs often become <a href="/wiki/Independent_politician" title="Independent politician">independents</a>.\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Michelle_Thomson" title="Michelle Thomson">Michelle Thomson</a> (SNP, <a href="/wiki/Edinburgh_West_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Edinburgh West (UK Parliament constituency)">Edinburgh West</a>)</li></ul>\n<dl><dd><table style="text-align:center">\n<tbody><tr>\n<td style="width:4px; background-color:#FEF987;" data-sort-value="Scottish National Party">\n</td>\n<td style="text-align:left;" scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Scottish_National_Party" title="Scottish National Party">SNP</a>\n</td>\n<td>\xe2\x86\x92\n</td>\n<td style="width:4px; background-color:#DDDDDD;" data-sort-value="Independent politician">\n</td>\n<td style="text-align:left;" scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Independent_politician" title="Independent politician">Independent</a>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2">\n</td>\n<td>29 September 2015\n</td>\n<td colspan="2">\n</td></tr></tbody></table></dd></dl>\n<dl><dd>Thomson withdrew from the SNP whip on 29 September 2015 after her business became the subject of a police investigation into alleged irregularities regarding property deals.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> As a result, she then sat as an independent. In line with party rules, upon withdrawing from the whip, her SNP membership was suspended.</dd></dl>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Natalie_McGarry" title="Natalie McGarry">Natalie McGarry</a> (SNP, <a href="/wiki/Glasgow_East_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Glasgow East (UK Parliament constituency)">Glasgow East</a>)</li></ul>\n<dl><dd><table style="text-align:center">\n<tbody><tr>\n<td style="width:4px; background-color:#FEF987;" data-sort-value="Scottish National Party">\n</td>\n<td style="text-align:left;" scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Scottish_National_Party" title="Scottish National Party">SNP</a>\n</td>\n<td>\xe2\x86\x92\n</td>\n<td style="width:4px; background-color:#DDDDDD;" data-sort-value="Independent politician">\n</td>\n<td style="text-align:left;" scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Independent_politician" title="Independent politician">Independent</a>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2">\n</td>\n<td>24 November 2015\n</td>\n<td colspan="2">\n</td></tr></tbody></table></dd></dl>\n<dl><dd>McGarry withdrew from the SNP whip on 24 November 2015 after being named as under investigation by the police regarding financial discrepancies relating to <a href="/wiki/Women_for_Independence" title="Women for Independence">Women for Independence</a>, a campaign organisation for which she is a founder.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> As a result, she then sat as an independent. In line with party rules, upon withdrawing from the whip, her SNP membership was suspended.</dd></dl>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Simon_Danczuk" title="Simon Danczuk">Simon Danczuk</a> (Labour, <a href="/wiki/Rochdale_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Rochdale (UK Parliament constituency)">Rochdale</a>)</li></ul>\n<dl><dd><table style="text-align:center">\n<tbody><tr>\n<td style="width:4px; background-color:#DC241f;" data-sort-value="Labour Party (UK)">\n</td>\n<td style="text-align:left;" scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Labour_Party_(UK)" title="Labour Party (UK)">Labour</a>\n</td>\n<td>\xe2\x86\x92\n</td>\n<td style="width:4px; background-color:#DDDDDD;" data-sort-value="Independent politician">\n</td>\n<td style="text-align:left;" scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Independent_politician" title="Independent politician">Independent</a>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2">\n</td>\n<td>31 December 2015\n</td>\n<td colspan="2">\n</td></tr></tbody></table></dd></dl>\n<dl><dd>Danczuk was suspended from the Labour Party on 31 December 2015, pending an investigation by the <a href="/wiki/National_Executive_Committee" title="National Executive Committee">National Executive Committee</a>, after allegations were made that he exchanged explicit messages with a 17-year-old girl. As a result of the suspension, he has been withdrawn from the Labour whip, and then sat as an independent.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup></dd></dl>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Naz_Shah" title="Naz Shah">Naz Shah</a> (Labour, <a href="/wiki/Bradford_West_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Bradford West (UK Parliament constituency)">Bradford West</a>)</li></ul>\n<dl><dd><table style="text-align:center">\n<tbody><tr>\n<td style="width:4px; background-color:#DC241f;" data-sort-value="Labour Party (UK)">\n</td>\n<td style="text-align:left;" scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Labour_Party_(UK)" title="Labour Party (UK)">Labour</a>\n</td>\n<td>\xe2\x86\x92\n</td>\n<td style="width:4px; background-color:#DDDDDD;" data-sort-value="Independent politician">\n</td>\n<td style="text-align:left;" scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Independent_politician" title="Independent politician">Independent</a>\n</td>\n<td>\xe2\x86\x92\n</td>\n<td style="width:4px; background-color:#DC241f;" data-sort-value="Labour Party (UK)">\n</td>\n<td style="text-align:left;" scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Labour_Party_(UK)" title="Labour Party (UK)">Labour</a>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2">\n</td>\n<td>27 April 2016\n</td>\n<td colspan="2">\n</td>\n<td>5 July 2016\n</td>\n<td colspan="2">\n</td></tr></tbody></table></dd></dl>\n<dl><dd>Shah was suspended from the Labour Party on 27 April 2016 pending an investigation into social media comments which she made, including proposing the relocation of <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israel</a> to North America. As a result of the suspension, she was withdrawn from the Labour whip and she sat as an independent,<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> before being reinstated on 5 July 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup></dd></dl>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Justin_Tomlinson" title="Justin Tomlinson">Justin Tomlinson</a> (Conservative, <a href="/wiki/North_Swindon_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="North Swindon (UK Parliament constituency)">North Swindon</a>)</li></ul>\n<dl><dd><table style="text-align:center">\n<tbody><tr>\n<td style="width:4px; background-color:#0087DC;" data-sort-value="Conservative Party (UK)">\n</td>\n<td style="text-align:left;" scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Conservative_Party_(UK)" title="Conservative Party (UK)">Conservative</a>\n</td>\n<td>\xe2\x86\x92\n</td>\n<td>Suspended\n</td>\n<td>\xe2\x86\x92\n</td>\n<td style="width:4px; background-color:#0087DC;" data-sort-value="Conservative Party (UK)">\n</td>\n<td style="text-align:left;" scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Conservative_Party_(UK)" title="Conservative Party (UK)">Conservative</a>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="3">\n</td>\n<td>11\xe2\x80\x9312 October 2016\n</td>\n<td colspan="3">\n</td></tr></tbody></table></dd></dl>\n<dl><dd>Tomlinson was suspended from the House of Commons from 11 to 12 October 2016 after a vote by MPs on 10 October 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> This was in accordance with a recommendation by the <a href="/wiki/Standards_and_Privileges_Committee" title="Standards and Privileges Committee">Privileges Committee</a> after it found that he had committed a contempt by disclosing a confidential draft report by the <a href="/wiki/Public_Accounts_Committee_(United_Kingdom)" title="Public Accounts Committee (United Kingdom)">Public Accounts Committee</a> to an employee of <a href="/wiki/Wonga.com" title="Wonga.com">Wonga.com</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup></dd></dl>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Douglas_Carswell" title="Douglas Carswell">Douglas Carswell</a> (UKIP, <a href="/wiki/Clacton_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Clacton (UK Parliament constituency)">Clacton</a>)</li></ul>\n<dl><dd><table style="text-align:center">\n<tbody><tr>\n<td style="width:4px; background-color:#70147A;" data-sort-value="UK Independence Party">\n</td>\n<td style="text-align:left;" scope="row"><a href="/wiki/UK_Independence_Party" title="UK Independence Party">UKIP</a>\n</td>\n<td>\xe2\x86\x92\n</td>\n<td style="width:4px; background-color:#DDDDDD;" data-sort-value="Independent politician">\n</td>\n<td style="text-align:left;" scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Independent_politician" title="Independent politician">Independent</a>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2">\n</td>\n<td>25 March 2017\n</td>\n<td colspan="2">\n</td></tr></tbody></table></dd></dl>\n<dl><dd>Carswell left UKIP on 25 March 2017, saying that he had left amicably to focus on local issues as the UK was certain to leave the EU.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> Former leader <a href="/wiki/Nigel_Farage" title="Nigel Farage">Nigel Farage</a> had previously called for Carswell to quit, saying that Carswell was actively working against UKIP.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> As a result, he then sat as an independent.</dd></dl>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span
